Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





A local Elevation of Privilege vulnerability has been discovered in the Google Update Service. This issue can be exploited to obtain SYSTEM privileges on devices that have Google Chrome, or possibly other Google products, installed. The only configuration that is not vulnerable is whenever a user installs Chrome with a low privilege user and does not accept the UAC-prompt in the setup menu. This means that all enterprise configurations in which the Chrome application is installed/pushed to the user from a centralised MDM solution are vulnerable.



<span class="line"><!---->A local Elevation of Privilege vulnerability has been discovered in the Google Update Service. This issue can be exploited to obtain SYSTEM privileges on devices that have Google Chrome, or possibly other Google products, installed. The only configuration that is not vulnerable is whenever a user installs Chrome with a low privilege user and does not accept the UAC-prompt in the setup menu. This means that all enterprise configurations in which the Chrome application is installed/pushed to the user from a centralised MDM solution are vulnerable.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 1.3.36.82 (Latest, stable)



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 1.3.36.82 (Latest, stable)<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Windows, all versions. Other operating systems have not been tested.



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Windows, all versions. Other operating systems have not been tested.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





The vulnerability is quiet straightforward. Whenever Chrome is being installed for all users two scheduled tasks are being created called "GoogleUpdateTaskMachineUA" and "GoogleUpdateTaskMachineCore. These tasks run as SYSTEM as is always the case when "Run whether user is logged on or not" is selected. These tasks are scheduled to run every hour. When the task is run, it checks for the file "GoogleUpdate.ini" on the C:\ root folder.



<span class="line"><!---->The vulnerability is quiet straightforward. Whenever Chrome is being installed for all users two scheduled tasks are being created called "GoogleUpdateTaskMachineUA" and "GoogleUpdateTaskMachineCore. These tasks run as SYSTEM as is always the case when "Run whether user is logged on or not" is selected. These tasks are scheduled to run every hour. When the task is run, it checks for the file "GoogleUpdate.ini" on the C:\ root folder.<!----></span>



<br>





In this file a user can specify several settings for debugging. One of these settings is the "LogFilePath" value. These settings are specified on your help pages (see: 



<span class="line"><!---->In this file a user can specify several settings for debugging. One of these settings is the "LogFilePath" value. These settings are specified on your help pages (see: <!----></span>





https://support.google.com/chrome/a/answer/6350036?hl=en#zippy=%2Cturn-on-auto-updates-recommended%2Cschedule-auto-updates-outside-of-work-hours%2Ccreate-a-log-file



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://support.google.com/chrome/a/answer/6350036?hl=en#zippy=%2Cturn-on-auto-updates-recommended%2Cschedule-auto-updates-outside-of-work-hours%2Ccreate-a-log-file"><!---->https://support.google.com/chrome/a/answer/6350036?hl=en#zippy=%2Cturn-on-auto-updates-recommended%2Cschedule-auto-updates-outside-of-work-hours%2Ccreate-a-log-file<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When only a filename is being specified the logfile will be written in C:\ProgramData\Google\Update\Log\.



<span class="line"><!---->When only a filename is being specified the logfile will be written in C:\ProgramData\Google\Update\Log\.<!----></span>



<br>





The problem is that a user can enter a full path here and also specify any filename and/or extension that they wish.



<span class="line"><!---->The problem is that a user can enter a full path here and also specify any filename and/or extension that they wish.<!----></span>



<br>





When the GoogleUpdate tasks are being executed two things will happen:



<span class="line"><!---->When the GoogleUpdate tasks are being executed two things will happen:<!----></span>



<br>





1. It checks whether the file exists. If it doesn't, the file will first be created. Then logentries will be appended to the file. 



<span class="line"><!---->1. It checks whether the file exists. If it doesn't, the file will first be created. Then logentries will be appended to the file. <!----></span>



<br>





2. The permissions of the file will be altered so that all users have write permissions towards the file.



<span class="line"><!---->2. The permissions of the file will be altered so that all users have write permissions towards the file.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This procedure is, naturally, being done using SYSTEM privileges. This means a user can abuse this to obtain write-permissions for every file they wish, independent of it's location.



<span class="line"><!---->This procedure is, naturally, being done using SYSTEM privileges. This means a user can abuse this to obtain write-permissions for every file they wish, independent of it's location.<!----></span>



<br>





This can exploited in numerours ways. If you want me to make a Proof of Concept in which I showcase that this can be abused to obtain a SYSTEM shell on the machine, I will be happy to do so.



<span class="line"><!---->This can exploited in numerours ways. If you want me to make a Proof of Concept in which I showcase that this can be abused to obtain a SYSTEM shell on the machine, I will be happy to do so.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I have attached a PDF with screenshots.



<span class="line"><!---->I have attached a PDF with screenshots.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





Reproduction steps:



<span class="line"><!---->Reproduction steps:<!----></span>



<br>





1. On your Windows computer, create a text file called GoogleUpdate.ini.



<span class="line"><!---->1. On your Windows computer, create a text file called GoogleUpdate.ini.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Save the file on the drive root, C:\.



<span class="line"><!---->2. Save the file on the drive root, C:\.<!----></span>



<br>





3. Include the content below (where the value of "LogFilePath" can be any file on the system):



<span class="line"><!---->3. Include the content below (where the value of "LogFilePath" can be any file on the system):<!----></span>



<br>





	[LoggingLevel]



<span class="line"><!---->	[LoggingLevel]<!----></span>



<br>





	LC_UTIL=6



<span class="line"><!---->	LC_UTIL=6<!----></span>



<br>





	LC_SERVICE=6



<span class="line"><!---->	LC_SERVICE=6<!----></span>



<br>





	LC_CORE=6



<span class="line"><!---->	LC_CORE=6<!----></span>



<br>





	LC_NET=6



<span class="line"><!---->	LC_NET=6<!----></span>



<br>





	LC_OPT=6



<span class="line"><!---->	LC_OPT=6<!----></span>



<br>





	[LoggingSettings]



<span class="line"><!---->	[LoggingSettings]<!----></span>



<br>





	EnableLogging=1



<span class="line"><!---->	EnableLogging=1<!----></span>



<br>





	ShowTime=1



<span class="line"><!---->	ShowTime=1<!----></span>



<br>





	LogToFile=1



<span class="line"><!---->	LogToFile=1<!----></span>



<br>





	AppendToFile=1



<span class="line"><!---->	AppendToFile=1<!----></span>



<br>





	LogToStdOut=1



<span class="line"><!---->	LogToStdOut=1<!----></span>



<br>





	LogToOutputDebug=1



<span class="line"><!---->	LogToOutputDebug=1<!----></span>



<br>





	LogFilePath=C:\Program Files (x86)\Google\Update\1.3.36.82\GoogleCrashHandler.exe



<span class="line"><!---->	LogFilePath=C:\Program Files (x86)\Google\Update\1.3.36.82\GoogleCrashHandler.exe<!----></span>



<br>





4. Wait for the GoogleUpdate task to run (this happens every hour). Or trigger it manually by executing the task for the PoC (requires admin privileges).



<span class="line"><!---->4. Wait for the GoogleUpdate task to run (this happens every hour). Or trigger it manually by executing the task for the PoC (requires admin privileges).<!----></span>



<br>





5. The specified LogFile is now created and the user has write permissions on it.



<span class="line"><!---->5. The specified LogFile is now created and the user has write permissions on it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I have attached a PDF with screenshots.



<span class="line"><!---->I have attached a PDF with screenshots.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Patch suggestion:



<span class="line"><!---->Patch suggestion:<!----></span>



<br>





The easiest solution would be to change the searchlocation of GoogleUpdate.ini to "C:\Program Files (x86)\Google\Update\".



<span class="line"><!---->The easiest solution would be to change the searchlocation of GoogleUpdate.ini to "C:\Program Files (x86)\Google\Update\".<!----></span>



<br>





Another easy solutions would be to completely remove the LogFilePath parameter in the logsettings file.



<span class="line"><!---->Another easy solutions would be to completely remove the LogFilePath parameter in the logsettings file.<!----></span>



<br>





Last solution would be to prohibit the usage of paths and different file extensions in the value of the LogFilePath parameter.



<span class="line"><!---->Last solution would be to prohibit the usage of paths and different file extensions in the value of the LogFilePath parameter.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





CREDIT INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->CREDIT INFORMATION<!----></b>

<span class="line"><!---->Reporter credit: Jan van der Put (REQON B.V.)<!----></span>

I think the default permissions on Windows prevent this at Step (2) above - standard users do not have permission to write to c:\ so cannot create this file. Are you sure you are running as a non-Admin (or non-UAC) context?



<span class="line"><!---->I think the default permissions on Windows prevent this at Step (2) above - standard users do not have permission to write to c:\ so cannot create this file. Are you sure you are running as a non-Admin (or non-UAC) context?<!----></span>

Hi, sorry for my delayed reply, I missed the notifcation. I’ve checked in a fresh Windows install and you seem to be correct that by default a low privileged user has no filecreate permissions on C:\.



<span class="line"><!---->Hi, sorry for my delayed reply, I missed the notifcation. I’ve checked in a fresh Windows install and you seem to be correct that by default a low privileged user has no filecreate permissions on C:\.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, and I still can’t figure out why, ALL the Windows configurations that I have reviewed for clients (20+ different configurations), all provide write permissions on C:\ for standard domain users. No exceptions.



<span class="line"><!---->However, and I still can’t figure out why, ALL the Windows configurations that I have reviewed for clients (20+ different configurations), all provide write permissions on C:\ for standard domain users. No exceptions.<!----></span>



<br>





So I thought this might had something to do with it being a domain joined PC, but in my local AD lab this is also not the case.



<span class="line"><!---->So I thought this might had something to do with it being a domain joined PC, but in my local AD lab this is also not the case.<!----></span>



<br>





Now i’m wondering if this has something to do with an enterprise AD management solution like SCCM. I’m currently trying to figure this out by trying to recreate the configuration on our clients. 



<span class="line"><!---->Now i’m wondering if this has something to do with an enterprise AD management solution like SCCM. I’m currently trying to figure this out by trying to recreate the configuration on our clients. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In any case, even though this might not be exploitable in an out-of-the-box windows installation. If this appears to be exploitable in most (if not all) enterprise AD configurations, then this does pose a serious risk caused by the GoogleUpdate service.



<span class="line"><!---->In any case, even though this might not be exploitable in an out-of-the-box windows installation. If this appears to be exploitable in most (if not all) enterprise AD configurations, then this does pose a serious risk caused by the GoogleUpdate service.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Could you maybe check if the permissions are configured like this in your enterprise AD environment? So not in a separate test-lab. I will also continue researching this myself.



<span class="line"><!---->Could you maybe check if the permissions are configured like this in your enterprise AD environment? So not in a separate test-lab. I will also continue researching this myself.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Kind regards,



<span class="line"><!---->Kind regards,<!----></span>

I've just contacted one of our client that does Windows Sysadmin interim jobs for a large number of clients, he confirmed that he has seen write access to C:\ in most configurations he has worked on. He states that this probably has something to do with Windows in combination with SCCM.



<span class="line"><!---->I've just contacted one of our client that does Windows Sysadmin interim jobs for a large number of clients, he confirmed that he has seen write access to C:\ in most configurations he has worked on. He states that this probably has something to do with Windows in combination with SCCM.<!----></span>



<br>





I will set up a test lab with SCCM this weekend in order to test this. SCCM is very commonly used and if this causes the change in write permissions this severely impacts the risk of this vulnerability.



<span class="line"><!---->I will set up a test lab with SCCM this weekend in order to test this. SCCM is very commonly used and if this causes the change in write permissions this severely impacts the risk of this vulnerability.<!----></span>

Hi, no not yet. I’m a little short on time. However, I was able to confirm some aspects.



<span class="line"><!---->Hi, no not yet. I’m a little short on time. However, I was able to confirm some aspects.<!----></span>



<br>





By default, in any Windows configuration, the special identity/group “Authenticated Users” has Write access to C:\. Every user that has authenticated through a sign-in process is part of this identity (



<span class="line"><!---->By default, in any Windows configuration, the special identity/group “Authenticated Users” has Write access to C:\. Every user that has authenticated through a sign-in process is part of this identity (<!----></span>





https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/identity-protection/access-control/special-identities#authenticated-users



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/identity-protection/access-control/special-identities#authenticated-users"><!---->https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/security/identity-protection/access-control/special-identities#authenticated-users<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>



<br>





However, the local group “Users” does not have Write access to C:\. I’m not sure what permissions overrule which. But I think the reason all my clients have write access is that they install the Windows OS without any local users and that users will sign-in to the OS using AD. I did not have this set-up ready in my local testlab.



<span class="line"><!---->However, the local group “Users” does not have Write access to C:\. I’m not sure what permissions overrule which. But I think the reason all my clients have write access is that they install the Windows OS without any local users and that users will sign-in to the OS using AD. I did not have this set-up ready in my local testlab.<!----></span>



<br>





I hope that I have time to confirm this upcoming weekend. Since I understand you want to take actions on this open issue, let’s agree upon the following timeline. I will provide you with an update before next Tuesday. If I can not confirm the reason for the Write access by then, we assume it’s not possible in ‘standard configuration’ and you can rate the issue from that perspective. Is this ok?



<span class="line"><!---->I hope that I have time to confirm this upcoming weekend. Since I understand you want to take actions on this open issue, let’s agree upon the following timeline. <br>


    


        


      


        









This is fixed in the GoogleUpdate codebase, and will be shipped with the next release which is expected to be sometime in June.



<span class="line"><!---->This is fixed in the GoogleUpdate codebase, and will be shipped with the next release which is expected to be sometime in June.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To mitigate this issue, the fix does the following:



<span class="line"><!---->To mitigate this issue, the fix does the following:<!----></span>



<br>





* removes the ability to specify a `LogFilePath` in GoogleUpdate.ini. This implies that the log file will always be GoogleUpdate.log and always under the %ALLUSERSPROFILE%\Google\Update\Log directory.



<span class="line"><!---->* removes the ability to specify a `LogFilePath` in GoogleUpdate.ini. This implies that the log file will always be GoogleUpdate.log and always under the %ALLUSERSPROFILE%\Google\Update\Log directory.<!----></span>



<br>





* checks whether the file is a reparse point after opening the file. The check is made after opening the file, so that the attacker does not get a chance to substitute a reparse point.



<span class="line"><!---->* checks whether the file is a reparse point after opening the file. The check is made after opening the file, so that the attacker does not get a chance to substitute a reparse point.<!----></span>



<br>





* as a defense in depth measure, we check to make sure the parent directory has not been redirected. i.e., the %ALLUSERSPROFILE%\Google\Update directory. We do not check %ALLUSERSPROFILE%\Google and above for reparse points, since an attacker would need to reuse an existing directory structure which has "\Update", which narrows the attack surface considerably, and in addition, we only write to a "GoogleUpdate.log" file within, which is unlikely to affect most applications (such as GoogleUpdate, which has that directory structure under %ProgramFiles (x86)%).



<span class="line"><!---->* as a defense in depth measure, we check to make sure the parent directory has not been redirected. i.e., the %ALLUSERSPROFILE%\Google\Update directory. We do not check %ALLUSERSPROFILE%\Google and above for reparse points, since an attacker would need to reuse an existing directory structure which has "\Update", which narrows the attack surface considerably, and in addition, we only write to a "GoogleUpdate.log" file within, which is unlikely to affect most applications (such as GoogleUpdate, which has that directory structure under %ProgramFiles (x86)%).<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
